        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer191241669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4080656822247658748"><b>
  <blockquote>I’d rather be miserable loving you than happy with anyone else.</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>3 and a half stars<br/><br/>Basic plot:<br/>Girl is "ugly" but is a beautiful singer. Choir group gives her makeover. "Hot" guy from another choir falls in love with her. Dark secret, etc.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>What I liked about this book:</u>
</b><br/>-It was cheesy but it still managed to be likeable and it kept my interest. <br/>-The last 50 or so pages had me in tears, so obviously it was good at tugging at the heartstrings.<br/>-The best friend. I liked her best friend more than D</span>
  <span id="freeText4080656822247658748" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>I’d rather be miserable loving you than happy with anyone else.</blockquote>
</b><br /><br />3 and a half stars<br /><br />Basic plot:<br />Girl is "ugly" but is a beautiful singer. Choir group gives her makeover. "Hot" guy from another choir falls in love with her. Dark secret, etc.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>What I liked about this book:</u>
</b><br />-It was cheesy but it still managed to be likeable and it kept my interest. <br />-The last 50 or so pages had me in tears, so obviously it was good at tugging at the heartstrings.<br />-The best friend. I liked her best friend more than Derek. I liked Derek AT TIMES but Scott was more likeable in my eyes. <br />-The overall book had a sweet, sad overtone which was nicely done.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>What I didn't like about this book:</u>
</b><br />-Grace's makeover. It totally sends out the wrong message to girls. Plus it was completely obnoxious and unbelievable. In the beginning of the book, she describes herself as if she is hideous and her nickname in school is "The Beast". Then over a few weeks(I guess? I don't think the book made it clear how long the makeover took), she gets laser surgery to get rid of acne, a new haircut and laser eye surgery(which she seems to just get without a consultation; and you're supposed to be at LEAST over 18 years old to get Lasik. I got mine at 23 years old and my eyesight is already starting to regress a little.) And the girls in her choir group kind of teach her how to use a hair straightener and makeup.<br /><br />REALLY?! It's hard to stomach that she goes from being "ugly" to being attractive(which is shown in how many boys/men pay attention to her after the makeover.) Apparently, acne + bad hair + glasses = UGLY. Nice message, huh? <br /><br />-Derek's behaviour. I don't care why he did it the things he did. But the actual "relationship" between Derek and Beth wasn't exactly something to aspire to. Yes, the last 50 or so pages were nice but I was disappointed with the middle part of the book. Beth and Derek meet at a Choir competition in Switzerland and fall madly in love. And it's kind of sweet but mostly seems like Beth wants to jump his bones and Derek is like slooooooow dowwwwwn. <br /><br />Then they have to go back to their regular lives but promise to make the long distance relationship work. Which doesn't really work that well because of Derek. He has his reasons but he should've just been honest. You can't hide something so major from someone you say you love. <br /><br />-Beth's craziness. First of all, she is one of those "OMG I love him and can't live without him!" kind of girls. She is one of the neediest, clingiest girls I've read about in a long time. I know love is a powerful thing but I just kept picturing her as this psycho, constantly calling/messaging/texting her boyfriend. It was a little creepy.<br /><br />Plus, there was her best friend, Scott. Scott, who loved her before her makeover and continues to love her throughout the book. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I found it funny that she was so in love with Derek but when Scott went to kiss her, she was all "OMG! I luvz kissessss!" I don't believe you can be so in love with one person and willingly kiss another person. So that kind of ruined the credibility of the love she felt. Also the fact that she continued to have lusty feelings for her best friend throughout the book and at the end, falls right into Scott's waiting arms. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />-The love triangle. Love triangles are okay sometimes but they start to get old. Especially in these books where an awkward, ordinary girl suddenly has two guys who want her. And not just normal "Oh, I think she's cute. I want to date her." kind of want. The "I LOVE HER! I want to spend forever with her and I can't live without her!" kind of want.<br /><br />Which lets face it, it's hard to imagine many teenage boys actually being this intense.<br /><br />Oh, and also, there were aspects of Derek/Scott that reminded me of Edward/Jacob. <br />Derek/Edward: won't have sex with Beth even though she's throwing herself at him(<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and yes, there are reasons, but he should've told her why! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>), tells Beth maybe Scott would be better for her(doesn't Edward tell Bella that Jacob would be better for her?)<br />Scott/Jacob: Beth's best friend who she has lusty feelings for, more physical than Derek, more personality and charm than Derek.<br /><br />Also, Beth had similarities to Bella: insecure, needy, thinks her boyfriend is the most amazing boy ever, at one point says she'd die without him, etc. <br /><br />Just little things. I'm sure it was unintentional but the love triangle reminded me of Twilight at times. <br /><br />-I kept getting confused about where Derek was from! This is my own fault, really but here is why:<br />Beth said he's from London. I assumed London, England. Really it's London, Ontario but then Derek kept saying "mum" and at one part they sat in front of the Thames River. I was like "What?" Was the author deliberately trying to confuse me? I looked it up after and there is a Thames River in both London, England AND London, Ontario. However, a Canadian boy calling his mom "mum" is just fucked. Unless people in London, Ontario are trying to be as much like London, England as they can. <br />I'm Canadian but now that I'm in England, I call my mom "mum" as a jokey thing sometimes. I'm sure I was the only one confused by this aspect of the book and for that, I apologise. <br /><br />-The lyrics. I thought all the lyrics were so boring and contrived. It made me think of how amazing the lyrics were in "Where She Went" by Gayle Forman. The lyrics in "Sing Me To Sleep" just made me roll my eyes.<br /><br />Which reminds me, when I heard the title of this book, I immediately thought of The Smiths song "Asleep". <br /><i>
  <b>Sing me to sleep. Sing me to sleep. And then leave me alone. <br />Don't try to wake me in the morning cause I will be gone.<br />Don't feel bad for me I want you to know<br />Deep in the cell of my heart, I really want to go.</b>
</i><br />And I love that song so I thought there might be a connection. But no.<br />Oh wells. <br /><br />So basically, overall I had mixed feelings about this book. I liked it as a one-time read but it didn't make me love it. It did make me cry but I thought the actual writing was pretty cheesy. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I appreciate that this was loosely based on a true story and that's what made the ending so much harder for me to read. It made me terribly sad knowing people have to live with this terrible disease. I cried mostly because I couldn't help imagining if it were me or someone I love going through all of it.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I liked this book. I just didn't <i>love</i> it. I wanted to <i>love</i> it. I had high hopes for it. I don't know if it was the makeover that ruined it for me or something else but I just didn't like it as much as I'd hoped I would.<br /><br />This book did have it's good points and it kept me interested. I would recommend this to someone who likes ugly-duckling-turns-into-a-swan stories or anyone who loves Y.A contemporary romance. <br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>I needed a whole heart once in my life. Is that so wrong?</blockquote>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4080656822247658748" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8495697097801410625">I can't begin to say how much I LOVED THIS BOOK! It surpassed my expectations and is definetly one of the best love stories I have ever read. I laughed, I cried, I felt everything Beth and Derek were feeling for each other.<br/><br/>Though she lived her life on the sidelines, Beth suddenly found herself thrust into the spotlight when she is chosen to be the new soloist for her all girls choir. With her beautiful voice leading the way, Beth's group wins a spot to compete in the 'Choral Olympics' to be held</span>
  <span id="freeText8495697097801410625" style="display:none">I can't begin to say how much I LOVED THIS BOOK! It surpassed my expectations and is definetly one of the best love stories I have ever read. I laughed, I cried, I felt everything Beth and Derek were feeling for each other.<br /><br />Though she lived her life on the sidelines, Beth suddenly found herself thrust into the spotlight when she is chosen to be the new soloist for her all girls choir. With her beautiful voice leading the way, Beth's group wins a spot to compete in the 'Choral Olympics' to be held in Switzerland.<br /><br />That's when the other girls in the choir decide to give Beth a make over. She receives special treatments for her face, highlights in her hair, and laser eye surgery to have perfect vision.<br /><br />Now her outter beauty matches her inner beauty, but Beth still can't shake the painful identity of 'the beast'. On her first day in Switzerland, Beth meets Derek. He's handsome, friendly, and also very talented in the singing department. Derek makes it no secret that he likes Beth, just by hearing her sing on her choir's website he was in love with her. At first Beth is doubtful that Derek's feelings are genuine, but when she gets bad news via the phone, Derek is there to comfort her. One minute they're sitting on a bench and she's crying on his shoulder, and the next they're making out!<br /><br />At that point I hugged the book, screamed a little, and then kept reading! With every page it got better and better. I fell in love with Derek just as much as Beth did! He opened her up and made her believe in herself like she never had before.<br /><br />It's been days since I finished reading, and I still can't stop thinking about it. It got to me in a way that very few books have. Anyone who reads it will be emotionally affected. I loved it so much that I would campaign for it to be a movie! If you go to the author's official website Angela Morrison - Sing me to sleep you can read the epilogue that she left out of the book. (But don't read it until you read the book.) There is also a link for the trailer, which is on youtube.</span>

<div id="review_88918729" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/88918729" />
    <a title="J.Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/208599-j-elle"><img alt="J.Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599186156p2/208599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/88918729?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.Elle" href="/user/show/208599-j-elle">J.Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/208599-j-elle?shelf=first-reads">first-reads</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer88918729&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer88918729" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer758964102453995658">I just cannot help but get the sense that more and more authors are grasping for that instant connection that Bella and Edward had in <br/>"Twilight". Now, I know there are lots of haters of that series and frankly, I HATED the last book and once the glow wore off the first book, I realized it's not the best written book I've ever read. However, I cannot deny that the connection Bella and Edward had really seemed real (as least it did to me). I can not say the same about this book. The description of</span>
  <span id="freeText758964102453995658" style="display:none">I just cannot help but get the sense that more and more authors are grasping for that instant connection that Bella and Edward had in <br />"Twilight". Now, I know there are lots of haters of that series and frankly, I HATED the last book and once the glow wore off the first book, I realized it's not the best written book I've ever read. However, I cannot deny that the connection Bella and Edward had really seemed real (as least it did to me). I can not say the same about this book. The description of the book said that it was about a girl, Beth, who is called "The Beast" because of her looks, until she is selected to sing the solo in her choir and recieves the "make-over of a lifetime." After her make-over, she goes on a trip with her choir and meets a boy, Derek, who changes her life. They fall in love in one day despite the fact that she still feels like she is "The Beast" and he seems to be hiding some dark secret. Well, it's not such a secret when I was able to figure out in a chapter that he was dying. Yet, Beth couldn't figure it out for months. Anyway, their "love" seemed contrived, as did Beth's anguish over realizing she might kind of be in love with her best friend, Scott, too. This book is liberally peppered with song lyrics; a fact that I found wearying. However, despite all this, my eyes <i>may</i> have gone a little misty when Derek did finally die. And the fact that I won this galley for free off of the Goodreads first-reads give-aways was quite exciting. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_155234915" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/155234915" />
    <a title="Zemira (Kylo Ren fangirl) Warner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4995937-zemira-kylo-ren-fangirl-warner"><img alt="Zemira (Kylo Ren fangirl) Warner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512674314p2/4995937.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155234915?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zemira (Kylo Ren fangirl) Warner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zemira (Kylo Ren fangirl) Warner" href="/user/show/4995937-zemira-kylo-ren-fangirl-warner">Zemira (Kylo Ren fangirl) Warner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9920588-sing-me-to-sleep">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone who is willing to cry a lot</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4995937-zemira-kylo-ren-fangirl-warner?shelf=realistic">realistic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4995937-zemira-kylo-ren-fangirl-warner?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4995937-zemira-kylo-ren-fangirl-warner?shelf=music">music</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4995937-zemira-kylo-ren-fangirl-warner?shelf=triangle-of-bermuda">triangle-of-bermuda</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4995937-zemira-kylo-ren-fangirl-warner?shelf=death">death</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155234915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4815937880530060236">This really is one of the most beautiful stories I have ever read. It had me laughing, and it had me crying. It had me feeling so low, I was effected when I put the book down, yet so happy and hopeful for myself, that it left me smiley and in a bit of a dreamy state. It's just impossible for me to put into words just how incredibly moving I found Sing Me to Sleep. This book has effected me so deeply, it will stay with me forever. Just beautiful. <br/><br/>It’s hard to say why this book made such the emoti</span>
  <span id="freeText4815937880530060236" style="display:none">This really is one of the most beautiful stories I have ever read. It had me laughing, and it had me crying. It had me feeling so low, I was effected when I put the book down, yet so happy and hopeful for myself, that it left me smiley and in a bit of a dreamy state. It's just impossible for me to put into words just how incredibly moving I found Sing Me to Sleep. This book has effected me so deeply, it will stay with me forever. Just beautiful. <br /><br />It’s hard to say why this book made such the emotionally impact it did on me. In part, it has to do with the character of Derek and what’s he’s hiding. What he goes though is so very heartbreaking, especially for Beth because just as she finds her inner beauty and strength, he must leave her. Angela shows with the character of Derek why some people are in our lives for only a short moment of time. Because Derek and Beth are so in love with one another, they are very intimate with one another. These two can’t stop kissing and touching. It’s handled very well, even when the topic of sex comes up. <br /><br />Sing Me to Sleep is a book you easily find yourself involved in, living. Toward the end of the story I felt like I was there, astonished by the actions of those around me, feeling the same feelings the characters were experiencing. The tears sliding down my face proved my involvement. <br /><br /><br />If anyone is interested,this is the song I was listening to <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=km_JvvizkBc">http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=km_Jvv...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4815937880530060236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_126625412" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/126625412" />
    <a title="Seena Seena " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2875657-seena-seena"><img alt="Seena Seena " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1304423151p2/2875657.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/126625412?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Seena Seena " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Seena Seena " href="/user/show/2875657-seena-seena">Seena Seena </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2875657-seena-seena?shelf=my-fav-s">my-fav-s</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

  <span id="freeText4573302090202199657" style="display:none">Requirements for being so ugly people call you "The Beast":<br /><br />1) terrible eyesight, thick glasses<br />2) being tall with long legs<br />3) acne<br />4) frizzy hair<br /><br />Guess what? <div id="review_107025722" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/107025722" />
    <a title="Joanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2084265-joanne"><img alt="Joanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600632902p2/2084265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107025722?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joanne" href="/user/show/2084265-joanne">Joanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2084265-joanne?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107025722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1758462254529029283"><i>THE TRANSFORMATION <br/>Beth has always been “The Beast”—that’s what everyone at school calls her because of her awkward height, facial scars, and thick glasses. Beth’s only friend is geeky, golden-haired Scott. That is, until she’s selected to be her choir’s soprano soloist, and receives the makeover that will change her life forever. <br/><br/>THE LOVE AFFAIR <br/>When Beth’s choir travels to Switzerland, she meets Derek: pale, brooding, totally dreamy. Derek’s untethered passion—for music, and for Beth—leaves he</i></span>
  <span id="freeText1758462254529029283" style="display:none"><i>THE TRANSFORMATION <br />Beth has always been “The Beast”—that’s what everyone at school calls her because of her awkward height, facial scars, and thick glasses. Beth’s only friend is geeky, golden-haired Scott. That is, until she’s selected to be her choir’s soprano soloist, and receives the makeover that will change her life forever. <br /><br />THE LOVE AFFAIR <br />When Beth’s choir travels to Switzerland, she meets Derek: pale, brooding, totally dreamy. Derek’s untethered passion—for music, and for Beth—leaves her breathless. Because in Derek’s eyes? She’s not The Beast, she’s The Beauty. <br /><br />THE IMPOSSIBLE CHOICE <br />When Beth comes home, Scott, her best friend in the world, makes a confession that leaves her completely torn. Should she stand by sweet, steady Scott or follow the dangerous, intense new feelings she has for Derek? <br /><br />THE HEARTBREAK <br />The closer Beth gets to Derek, the further away he seems. Then Beth discovers that Derek’s been hiding a dark secret from her …one that could shatter everything.</i> From Amazon US. <br /><br />I can't tell you how amazing this book was. Really. I went through so many emotions while reading this, and I'm just completely blown away by it. It's brilliant! It covers so many issues all in one heart-warming yet heart breaking story, it's just fantastic.<br /><br />Beth is known as "the Beast" at school. She's unusually tall, suffers with bad acne, and wears thick, beer-bottle classes. Not only is she bullied atrociously, but she knows the way her father reacted when she was born, commenting on her ugliness, and not staying in her life for very long. Her self-esteem is the lowest it could possibly be, and has only one friend, Scott. But the girl has a set of pipes on her, and with managing to get the solo spot in her choir, her life changes. <br /><br />Now we all know bullying is never, ever right, and that it's disgusting in all it's forms. I was bullied when I was younger, so I know how much it sucks. But what Beth has to go through is beyond anything I could ever have coped with. The pain, the humiliation, day after day, it's heart breaking. It upset me so much, that I actually cried. And what's worse, she believes every word the bullies say. She looks in the mirror, and sees the Beast. Fortunately for us as readers, as the story progresses, we don't get to read too many bullying incidents, but it's with Beth, inthe back of her mind, the whole time. Even after her transformation into this beautiful young girl, she self-esteem is still low, and believes she will always be the Beast no matter how she looks, because that's who she is; the person she is. It's just so, so sad. <br /><br />But along comes Derek; absolutely gorgeous, and unbelievably lovely, and rock star of his own choir, he sees in Beth what only one other person - Scott - has. Beth doesn't trust him at first, and to be honest, neither did I - a guy that hot saying all the right things? He's obviously just sweet-talking to get what he wants. But he fell for her before he even met her, before he even saw her. He fell for her voice, and the soul she brings to her singing. He sews the seed which sparks Beth's realisation of who she actually is, and that beauty is so much more than just skin deep. Yes, he is just as amazing as he sounds - I'm actually getting choked up as I write this, remembering what he does for her. <br /><br />Their relationship, like all relationships, isn't all plain sailing. There are so many rocky patches, it's hard on both of them. Derek has a secret, and they both know it. He's vague, won't talk about things, and has long absences of no contact. Because her self-esteem is practically non-existant, Beth jumps to conlusions, some extreme conlusions, and gets insanely jealous. Derek can sometimes be demanding and controling, and Beth can sometimes be clingy and obsessive, or too forgiving and understanding. Beth's behaviour is annoying, but you can understand the reasons for it, and as the story unfolds and you find out about Derek, his behaviour is also understandable. But on the whole, their is just so, so sweet. <br /><br />There's also Scott. He's been Beth's friend forever. An outside like she is, he used to suffer because of his appearance, his geekiness, and for defending her. But he ends up growing out of acne and weedy frame, and starts getting sexy. People notice, Beth notices. Yet Scott noticed Beth years ago, back when she was the Beast. Like Derek, he sees Beth for who she is, he always has. He's just the sweetest guy, and he finally gains the courage to do something about how he feels when Derek comes onto the scene. It's a case of who will Beth choose in the end? <br /><br />I have to say, I worked out Derek's secret at the very beginning. I don't know if this makes the book predictable, or just means I'm good at working things out. Either way, I didn't get all the details, and there is a twist beyond anything I would have I expected. It left me reeling, completely. But looking back, and knowing now what I know about the story, there's no other way it could have ended. <br /><br />This really is one of the most beautiful stories I have ever read. It had me laughing, and it had me crying. It had me feeling so low, I was effected when I put the book down, yet so happy and hopeful for myself, that it left me smiley and in a bit of a dreamy state. It's just impossible for me to put into words just how incredibly moving I found Sing Me to Sleep. This book has effected me so deeply, it will stay with me forever. Just beautiful. I seriously cannot wait to read more of Angela Morrison's novels. <br /><br />This review is part of the Sing Me to Sleep Tour on <a href="http://internationalbooktours.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">International Blog Tours</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1758462254529029283" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_70870376" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/70870376" />
    <a title="Kym McNabney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2723482-kym-mcnabney"><img alt="Kym McNabney" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/70870376?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kym McNabney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kym McNabney" href="/user/show/2723482-kym-mcnabney">Kym McNabney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70870376" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7385261922118291310">SING ME TO SLEEP, WINS MY HEART<br/> <br/>Wow, where do I begin. I was blown away when I read TAKEN BY STORM by Angela Morrison’s, so I had no doubt, SING ME TO SLEEP would be good. Yet I couldn’t have begun to foresee what an impact Beth’s story would have on me.<br/> <br/>When I finish reading a book, I often run to the computer to write my review. Not so with SING ME TO SLEEP. There was no way I was emotionally ready after finishing the final pages. Heck, I wouldn’t have been able to see the screen, anyway.<br/> <br/>I wa</span>
  <span id="freeText7385261922118291310" style="display:none">SING ME TO SLEEP, WINS MY HEART<br /> <br />Wow, where do I begin. I was blown away when I read TAKEN BY STORM by Angela Morrison’s, so I had no doubt, SING ME TO SLEEP would be good. Yet I couldn’t have begun to foresee what an impact Beth’s story would have on me.<br /> <br />When I finish reading a book, I often run to the computer to write my review. Not so with SING ME TO SLEEP. There was no way I was emotionally ready after finishing the final pages. Heck, I wouldn’t have been able to see the screen, anyway.<br /> <br />I was pre-warned that I would need a box of tissues. Silently I said to myself, I don’t think so. As an avid reader, I’ve read my share of tearjerkers. One tissue, maybe…but a box? I don’t think so. <br /> <br />I couldn’t have been more wrong. <br /> <br />As an aspiring writer, I was in awe of Ms. Morrison’s writing as I read one great line after another. There was nothing I would have changed and that’s saying a lot. It exceeded anything I could have conjured up. She has a uniquely amazing way with words. Each line was perfect in every way. I laughed. I cried. I was angry. I smiled. I felt every emotion Beth, Derek, and Scott experienced. I felt as though I were right there in the midst of their lives <br /> <br />On page 88, my jaw dropped. Some of the sweetest words you could image came from Derek and Scott. Ms. Morrison is more then a writer of fiction. She’s a poet and a song writer as well. I was so caught up in the story that I longed for a soundtrack of, SING ME TO SLEEP. <br /> <br />I was taken back to my school days, living them through Beth and Scott. Many faces came to mind of past schoolmates. Kids today need to hear this story, as do teachers and parents. <br /> <br />SING ME TO SLEEP is filled with trials, and tribulations, as well as friendship, love, hope and faith. It was moving, gripping and intense. It set me on an emotional rollercoaster from the very first line to the very last! <br /> <br />I have never experience a book such as SING ME TO SLEEP where I sensed what direction the author was taking the characters early on, then doubted my decision several times, then was blown away by the final chapters.<br /> <br />This morning after the kids left for school and my husband for work, I sat down in the living room to read the remaining seventy pages. God must have known I would need the solitude. I began to read and couldn’t put it down. There were moments where I was chocked up but I kept reading, absorbing every word. <br /> <br />I held back my emotions…until I got to page 291. That’s were I lost it! I have never HAD to step away from a book before. After several long minutes, I was finally able to pull myself together enough to read the final pages. This was not the first time I’ve cried or got caught up in a book but NEVER to this capacity. I was an emotional wreck through the last three chapters. They were truly the most powerful chapters I’ve ever read. <br /> <br />This book is a must read for preteen, teens, young adults, teachers, parents, and so many more. One can not help but get caught up in the lives of these characters, each one beautifully done. I savored and absorbed every word, often rereading many lines because they were that good. <br /> <br />I see “movie” written all over this book. If some producer doesn’t snatch it up, they’ll be missing a great opportunity. <br /> <br />Watch out, Nicholas Sparks. <br /> <br />Reviewed by Kym McNabney <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7385261922118291310" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1465022206937202291">I had really mixed feelings about this book. The story, I liked. Really liked. The start was a bit clunky with the 'transformation' and everything, but after it really got into the story, I was happy. Obviously the ending was heartbreaking. I didn't cry, but it was pretty sad.<br/><br/><br/>The part I didn't like was the characters. Not all of them, most were okay, just the main ones, the ones who totally make the book, that's all. I actually liked Derrick for most of it, not just because of the end, because I</span>
  <span id="freeText1465022206937202291" style="display:none">I had really mixed feelings about this book. The story, I liked. Really liked. The start was a bit clunky with the 'transformation' and everything, but after it really got into the story, I was happy. Obviously the ending was heartbreaking. I didn't cry, but it was pretty sad.<br /><br /><br />The part I didn't like was the characters. Not all of them, most were okay, just the main ones, the ones who totally make the book, that's all. I actually liked Derrick for most of it, not just because of the end, because I saw it coming around about the time Beth should have, right at the start. He was moody and all the that, but I didn't really get this dangerous side he was supposed to have except for a small glimpse. I thought he was quite sweet.<br /><br />Now Scott. Scottie. Dickhead. He was SUPPOSED to be sweet. Bullshit. I get it at the start when Beth is still the Beast that not many guys, almost no guy, would be that nice. But when she comes back, she has a boyfriend that she is in love with and who is in love with her, he really couldn't give a shit, because Scottie isn't happy. If he was this amazing best friend, he would have been happy for her, let her know he was always there for her and ummmm, maybe, I don't know, not try to seduce her into cheating on her boyfriend literally every time he saw her. His motivations seemed really selfish, he wanted the girl, nevermind it's not what she wants and it's killing her to hurt him.<br />In love triangles, there is supposed to be the sweet romantic guy, and the guy who is pushy and tempting. Scott was meant to be the first guy and he totally wasn't. Out of the two, Derrick respected Beth's feelings more(although it didn't seem like it at times) and Scott was too stuck in his own world to do the same.<br /><br />Beth...how quick can girls turn weird and stalkery? Seriously, record speed. I know they had this awesome, romantic, book-worthy romance in Lausanne, which I liked, but she always sounded so desperate after they got home. I know she has crippled self esteem, but her paranoia and unrealistic neediness made her hard to sympathise with at times. Every time Derrick backed away the tiniest bit and they couldn't be together, she would scramble and just lose it.<br />The part at the start with Colby, I hope that doesn't actually happen at schools. If three guys are restraining a girl in the middle of a school, dude, call the cops. I just didn't buy that, felt like it was written for the convenience of the story. <br /><br />Also, the drug habit thing? Really? Is Beth that naive? He was always pale and coughing and sick, wounds that didn't really heal, and the only reason that she thought drugs was because of one little joking comment from Blake. I'll admit, I didn't pick CF(I thought maybe AIDS), but still, it looked like it was just a way to build Derrick up to be the bad boy he never seemed to be.<br /><br /><br /><br />Parts that I really liked, but in the end, too much that was convenient to the story but didn't really fit. The characters annoyed me and seemed maybe a little one dimensional, especially Scott.<br /><br />Also, anyone with tips for me on how to write more positive and much much shorter reviews, please let me know :)</span>

<div id="review_99498694" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Stormi (BMReviewsohmy)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/979193-stormi-bmreviewsohmy"><img alt="Stormi (BMReviewsohmy)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1433289344p2/979193.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/99498694?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stormi (BMReviewsohmy)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stormi (BMReviewsohmy)" href="/user/show/979193-stormi-bmreviewsohmy">Stormi (BMReviewsohmy)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer99498694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15096187745267446337">First off I would like to say that there is one thing I don't like to do and that is CRY! I really hate sappy love stories that end up making your cry at the end of the book. This is why I have never read a Nicholas Sparks book. Though I didn't actually cry I almost did and that is just as bad..lol So I have a warning for those who are like me. It is a very heart warming story though, I must give it that. :)<br/><br/>Warning!! This book will probably make you cry!<br/><br/>I am a sucker for Beauty and the Beast typ</span>
  <span id="freeText15096187745267446337" style="display:none">First off I would like to say that there is one thing I don't like to do and that is CRY! I really hate sappy love stories that end up making your cry at the end of the book. This is why I have never read a Nicholas Sparks book. Though I didn't actually cry I almost did and that is just as bad..lol So I have a warning for those who are like me. It is a very heart warming story though, I must give it that. :)<br /><br />Warning!! This book will probably make you cry!<br /><br />I am a sucker for Beauty and the Beast type stories and I thought Sing Me To Sleep was a unique take on the story. Beth, never knew what it was like to be pretty. Her own father called her ugly. She had just one friend who seen her as a person, Scott. <br /><br />This book has great characters that you can really feel for and even relate too. Beth, has a beautiful voice and loves to sing. She love to write lyrics and you can tell that music is her way of escaping reality. It was real interesting to see how she adapts to being attractive to a guy. Scott, is the faithful and loveable best friend. His only problem is that he is in love with his BF, but she just doesn't see it. I felt really sorry for Scott as he loved Beth and had to watch her be with Derek. Now Derek, I will be honest I wanted to hate him, I really did. I liked Scott and I didn't want Beth to be with Derek. I wanted him to be a druggie, so she would dump him. Derek, though was a really nice guy. I pretty much guessed what was wrong with him from the start, I just wanted it to be something else. His only fault was not letting Beth know what was wrong with him till the end. Over all he really was a sweet guy and I just couldn't be mad at him though I wanted too.<br /><br />The one thing I couldn't stand about this book was how clingy the author made Beth be. I know that Derek is Beths first boyfriend and maybe she really didn't know how to act around the opposite sex, but it drove me crazy. She would get mad when he didn't want her to come over, she was even willing to drive a hour in the middle of the night just so she could kiss him, and hold him, etc. UGH, I just wanted to smack her for it. <br /><br /><br />Sing Me To Sleep was a very witty, dramatic, sappy love story that reminds me a lot of Nicholas Sparks books. Over all it was a good story and if you love those books that make you sigh and cry, then you will like this book.<br /></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/404409211" />

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9752625-sandra?shelf=liked-the-characters-some-or-all">liked-the-characters-some-or-all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9752625-sandra?shelf=sad">sad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9752625-sandra?shelf=nooo-way">nooo-way</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9752625-sandra?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9752625-sandra?shelf=love-triangles">love-triangles</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer404409211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5690351434573018651">Sing me to sleep is about a 17 year old girl called Beth. Beth's life is kinda really lonely and miserable because every one is either scared or disgusted of her. She's been called ugly her whole life. In school they call her beast and bully her constantly. In the library ( where she works at summer) the little kids are scared of her. Her only friend is Scott ( a boy she have been best friends with since 3rd grade). Then one day she goes to choir and surprisingly volunteers to be the soloist for</span>
  <span id="freeText5690351434573018651" style="display:none">Sing me to sleep is about a 17 year old girl called Beth. Beth's life is kinda really lonely and miserable because every one is either scared or disgusted of her. She's been called ugly her whole life. In school they call her beast and bully her constantly. In the library ( where she works at summer) the little kids are scared of her. Her only friend is Scott ( a boy she have been best friends with since 3rd grade). Then one day she goes to choir and surprisingly volunteers to be the soloist for a song that no girls in the group can sing. The choir sounds so good with her as a soloist that they get in for the Choral Olympics. Then she receives a total makeover. <br /><br />When they arrive at Choral Olympics Beth meets this boy called Derek, who sings as well. They get to know each other more after that and then get more close. But the closer Beth gets to him the further away he seems. She knows he is keeping something from her. He looks paler and thinner, and sometimes just disappears without a word for a few weeks or days. And the worst thing of all, when she returns home Scott makes a confession that leaves her breathless.<br /><br /><br />The book started really well. I really enjoyed it. It was a unique, memorable, well written and heartbreaking story. It kept me curious and guessing all the way through. <br /><br />The characters were really interesting and i felt really connected with Beth, Derek and Scott. They were described really well but there wasn't much information about them. My favorite character is Derek, he is just so mysterious and romantic.<br /><br />Sing Me To Sleep is so different from other books for so many reasons. At the end i was crying like a baby! And that's hard. Out of all my books only 1 made me cry before i read Sing Me To Sleep. I'm still a bit upset over what happened at the end. I thought that Beth's father would show up and they would be a family or something, and that's why i would cry. But nope. The ending took me by surprise. However, i felt like the book ended too soon. I was really hoping Beth's father WOULD show up. I was actually a bit disappointed when he didn't. And i guess that's why i gave it 4 stars.<br /><br />Overall, Sing Me To Sleep is a beautifully heart wrenching story that shows what real love and loss means. definitely recommend it. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5690351434573018651" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_89422683" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/89422683" />
    <a title="Sherry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3185148-sherry"><img alt="Sherry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1336265486p2/3185148.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/89422683?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sherry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sherry" href="/user/show/3185148-sherry">Sherry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone/everyone</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Sherry by: </span>
      Angela Morrison
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer89422683" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14397667152269240639">First off, I have to admit that this isn't the type of book I usually read. Most of the books on my shelves contain some level of paranormal activity/creatures, mythology or something of that sort. I have been thinking about what I would say in this reivew all morning. To come up with words to describe this book just isn't possible, but i'll give it a try. Exciting, romantic, heartbreaking, breathtaking are just a few words that come to mind when I think of the brilliance that is Sing Me to Slee</span>
  <span id="freeText14397667152269240639" style="display:none">First off, I have to admit that this isn't the type of book I usually read. Most of the books on my shelves contain some level of paranormal activity/creatures, mythology or something of that sort. I have been thinking about what I would say in this reivew all morning. To come up with words to describe this book just isn't possible, but i'll give it a try. Exciting, romantic, heartbreaking, breathtaking are just a few words that come to mind when I think of the brilliance that is Sing Me to Sleep. I wanted to be able to tell you all how this book made me feel. I don't know if its because I don't usually read books like this, or what but something about it just grabbed me and never let me go, and it still hasn't. I've been thinking about the characters in this story, the changes in them, everything about it, since I stopped reading it at 11:30 last night. I can't say much without giving away a spoiler so I will keep this review short and simple. I want everyone who reads it to feel like I did after I read it. I felt such raw emotion, and I don't know the last time I truly felt this way after reading a book. I get extremely excited about some books that I love, and I get into the emotions of those books, but something in the way Angela writes makes me feel like i'm going through what those characters are going through. I don't have enough good things to say about it, so I guess I just recommend that you pick this book up when it is released. You won't regret it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14397667152269240639" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Grrr...<br/>It really just pissed me off, seriously.<br/>I hated her character.<br/>I also hated Derek for most of the book.<br/>What was his plan?   <span id="freeText5845892209239576455" style="display:none">What is wrong with these people?<br />Beth is so whiny and self-pitying.<br />And she's so dependent on Derek.<br />I mean, she barely knows the guy<br />and she goes on and on about how much<br />she HAS to be with him, or she doesn't<br />feel complete, she feels empty inside.<br />I hate girls like that, who completely<br />cling to the guys. I had high hopes for Scott.<br />And then he messed it all up. <br />He turns into a jerk, and he's making out with<br />other girls, and he's just not there for her, I guess.<br />It also bugged me how the parents didn't seem<br />to care what the heck trouble their kids got into.<br />They're sitting there in the living room, <br />making out like crazy and her mom doesn't even care.<br />What the heck?!?<br />Honestly, the only redeeming quality of this book<br />was the cover, which I really like.<br />Other than that, I was just constantly angry at<br />all the characters and the stupid things they were doing.<br />The end was super dumb too.<br />Honestly? They guy you "loved so much" just died,<br />and you're saying to another guy, "you were never second."<br />What the heck is wrong with this girl?!!!</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19571964-sing-me-to-sleep">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16791267-nerea-nieto?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16791267-nerea-nieto?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16791267-nerea-nieto?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16791267-nerea-nieto?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1100830783" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4105011148185028617">No. I know the author's intentions were right, but I can't stand a sick love like this and pretend it's ok.<br/>Derek was a manipulative an controlling guy and Beth was a girl with low self esteem who grew too dependent of him.<br/>Is that the vision of love that I want young readers to learn? No.<br/>I enjoyed the reading, I did, but Derek was so creepy the whole time and I didn't mind about his secret and everything, he still had this abusive personality that I couldn't forget about.<br/>And Beth? I thought that </span>
  <span id="freeText4105011148185028617" style="display:none">No. I know the author's intentions were right, but I can't stand a sick love like this and pretend it's ok.<br />Derek was a manipulative an controlling guy and Beth was a girl with low self esteem who grew too dependent of him.<br />Is that the vision of love that I want young readers to learn? No.<br />I enjoyed the reading, I did, but Derek was so creepy the whole time and I didn't mind about his secret and everything, he still had this abusive personality that I couldn't forget about.<br />And Beth? I thought that she'd learn something from this whole "The Beast" situation, that she'd learn that looks are not the most important thing. But she didn't. She had self esteem problems and when her appearance changes, then, all of a sudden, her life is great. No. Is that the message we want to learn? She learnt nothing from the whole situation.<br />Besides that, I found annoying the number of times the author confuses "you're" for "your". English is not my mother tongue, but even I notice this kind of things...</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1677hjFcJMQyjkVP3zPb7UEwy/01gnkELMyHtLMsplZfoAzixekQqPmYvtHz7jQCRhngPng13kQi/9IoyLy6+A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HFGmVR8v8L/HwahW/j704XmVRytRZSCA8jCrlH93ZTSUX1Ex65rE0wzXU8jS4xsOfrxs6BzSh8D8A/4IBOd5mg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
